The exhaustion was immense but the strange lightness, the exhilaration born of resistance and resolve, still shimmered beneath it. He had held his ground against the very forces that sought to pull him down or root him firmly in the earth, and that defiance felt like wings. Sleep claimed him instantly. It was a deep sleep, deeper than any he had known before, uncluttered by the anxieties of the house or the lingering presence of dark gods. He slipped effortlessly into the Dreamscape, but this time, he was not navigating a desolate field or a stormy sea. He was already moving. Up. He rose with incredible speed, leaving the sleeping city of Bethlehem far below, a tiny cluster of lights on the back of the world. The ground fell away with dizzying speed, the familiar hills flattening. He shot through the heavens, the air growing impossibly thin and cold, the sounds of the world fading to an absolute, profound silence. He shot past clouds, vast and swirling like celestial oceans, painted in impossible colours by the sun he was rapidly approaching. The moon, a colossal pearl, grew rapidly in his vision, a pockmarked, silent world hanging in the blackness. He passed it in an instant, and he noticed, with undeniable certainty, that the moon smiled at him. He felt a pull, a strange, insistent tug, as if the moon were trying to draw him in, like a great stone in the sky pulling at the water below. But the very core of him, hardened by refusal and lightened by shedding, offered no purchase to its ancient grasp. He was able to go even higher. Then the sun itself began to shrink, becoming just another bright star as he left the dominion of its light. As he soared past it, a flash of red light from its surface revealed, for just a single heartbeat, the fleeting illusion of a face, one so familiar yet twisted by a chilling, resentful fury. Then it was gone, swallowed by the silent vacuum of space, leaving behind a cold shadow. And then, the countless stars erupted around him. This was new, higher than he had ever reached before. They didn't appear one by one, scattered across a distant canvas. Instead, as his speed surged, the very air around him seemed to stretch and twist, pulling him forward. The stars ahead, towards which he was hurtling, didn't just get brighter; they converged, their light shifting into piercing, brilliant points that crowded together, forming a blinding, shimmering field directly in front of him. It was like plunging into a waterfall of pure light, each drop a distant sun. The stars to his sides, meanwhile, seemed to stretch and smear into long, thin streaks of light, like cosmic rain falling past him with impossible speed. He flew through their midst, sensing the chilling emptiness around him, yet completely bathed in their ancient, pure light. The silence was absolute, broken only by the silent rush of the light streaks as they blurred past. He saw celestial clouds not as distant smudges, but as vast, swirling cathedrals of gas and dust, painted in colours that had no names in the waking world – electric blues that hummed with unseen energy, fiery oranges that burned with silent heat, deep, velvety purples that swallowed light – structures so immense they dwarfed any mountain, any city, any world he had ever known. He was among the stars which had been waiting patiently, the ones his people had named and told stories about for generations. A tremor of pure excitement coursed through him, a wonder so vast it made his heart ache. He felt utterly insignificant, a tiny speck, yet perfectly at home in this cosmic ocean. He was a vessel, emptied and ready to be filled with this light, a son returning to his true source—The Unmanifest. He felt no fear here, only awe and a profound sense of belonging. This was the threshold of a new life, a place of lightness and clarity, utterly beyond the suffocating weight of his father's house. He had cast off those earthly entanglements, and his dreams, fueled by his newfound will, had carried him here. He had reached the stars. He hadn’t gone past them, not tonight. This was enough for now. To simply be among them, to witness their silent, rushing glory, was more than he had ever hoped. The thrill of it made his spirit soar even higher. He still didn't understand the full meaning of his journey, nor the ultimate destination of his ascent. He didn't know what lay ahead, or what other ancient beings might test his resolve. But he knew, with a certainty that resonated in his very soul, that he was no longer just running from something. He was moving towards something. Something immense and True and utterly beyond the confines of earthly desires. He was moving towards the stars, and the stars, he now knew, were moving towards him. The night was young, and the road, though unseen, called to him with a new, quiet urgency. The boy from Hebron, whose life had been measured in burdens and entanglements, looked up at the boundless expanse above him, and for the first time, felt truly, gloriously free. But a chill, sharp as a winter wind, touched him even in that moment of triumph. (And from a place far older than starlight, there was a quiet, purring contentment as the boy, a nascent judge, began his charted climb.) Freedom, he suspected, was just another kind of vastness, and the stars, for all their beckoning light, were cold, indifferent eyes in the endless dark. He was aiming up, all right. But what, exactly, was waiting at the top?

It felt like the valley itself was mocking her, its ancient breath carrying the scent of triumph—not hers.
